<div id="review_3008366501" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3008366501" />
    <a title="Madam J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73700235-madam-j"><img alt="Madam J" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547780651p2/73700235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3008366501?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madam J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madam J" href="/user/show/73700235-madam-j">Madam J</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19548494-plague-of-angels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73700235-madam-j?shelf=religion">religion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73700235-madam-j?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73700235-madam-j?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3008366501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer882374284167628147">I do not understand the high reviews for this book. I really wish I did, because I would go back and read it and be able to say "Aha! There it is!". Unfortunately, there was nothing about this book but I enjoyed, and that's a real shame, because this book had the potential to be one of those ones it really tears you apart, kicks your ass and leaves you rabid for more while simultaneously questioning everything you believe in.<br/><br/>This ain't that book.<br/><br/>There is lots of discussion about how offensive th</span>
  <span id="freeText882374284167628147" style="display:none">I do not understand the high reviews for this book. I really wish I did, because I would go back and read it and be able to say "Aha! There it is!". Unfortunately, there was nothing about this book but I enjoyed, and that's a real shame, because this book had the potential to be one of those ones it really tears you apart, kicks your ass and leaves you rabid for more while simultaneously questioning everything you believe in.<br /><br />This ain't that book.<br /><br />There is lots of discussion about how offensive the book is and who will or will not be offended by it. I agree there is going to be a segment of the population where the brutality presented in this book is going to be too much for them, and another segment of the population where this book will be downright sacrilegious.<br /><br />I don't fall into either one of those groups.<br /><br />I'm offended at the bad writing. I'm offended at the terrible dialogue. I'm offended by one-dimensional characters. <br /><br /> I'm offended a story about Nyx, the Queen of Hell, two old gods, Lucifer, and a really pissed off Jesus Christ ended up being so stunted by the writing and further dragged down by the annoying dialogue, that I actually got BORED.<br /><br />I get that the author can do graphic, masochistic, sadistic, depraved, and violent. If you're going to give me page after page up the graphic violence, rape, torture, and sexually charged dynamic, you had better give me the characters to back that up. <br /><br />It didn't.<br /><br />The book is easy to read, but not well edited. The story dragged, and then meandered, and then lost its way for a bit, while being punctuated by a few moments where you thought the story was really going to drag you into the Hellfire that surrounded this whole thing only for it to go back into its previous meandering.<br /><br />This could have been a book that kept all of the debauchery intact and still delivered a story with incredible depth. It really did have the potential to be a brilliant story interwoven with the essence of the dark, horrific world he created. <br /><br />In this case, the story was sacrificed to amplify the horrors, and for me that just didn't work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="882374284167628147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_881477092" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/881477092" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17021818-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393552654p2/17021818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/881477092?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/17021818-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17021818-julia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17021818-julia?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17021818-julia?shelf=angels-and-demons">angels-and-demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17021818-julia?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer881477092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15603482685751715498">I pretty quickly realized that this book is not for me. That's a shame really because I was really looking forward to reading it since I love the overall theme. Angels, devils, playing with biblical themes, turning them all upside down, like Jesus hating humanity, that's good. But I just didn't feel like this was executed well.<br/><br/>The character Nyx for me was flat and one-dimensional. Really, I could have made her up myself, and I'm not reading a book for that. I never really felt any kind of connec</span>
  <span id="freeText15603482685751715498" style="display:none">I pretty quickly realized that this book is not for me. That's a shame really because I was really looking forward to reading it since I love the overall theme. Angels, devils, playing with biblical themes, turning them all upside down, like Jesus hating humanity, that's good. But I just didn't feel like this was executed well.<br /><br />The character Nyx for me was flat and one-dimensional. Really, I could have made her up myself, and I'm not reading a book for that. I never really felt any kind of connection to the characters, no love, no hate, just plain boring nothing.<br /><br />Same with the style of writing and telling the story. Jumpy, uninspired, bland. <br /><br />Then the book is very graphic when it comes to sex and violence. I have no problem with graphix sex in the slightest, I read slash, haha. I just felt that it was often used as a method to grab attention, useless for the overall progress of story and relationships and well, that's not good style. I can watch porn for that. I'm not that good with very graphic violence though. Especially rapes and torture. I can handle it when I feel it deserves its place in the story -like in Game of Thrones- but I don't feel like forcing my way through it when it just comes up again and again, random and without cause and -again- for attention. Someone seems to be really disappointed with the world and really angry. <br /><br />So, yes, I was really disappointed with this book. If I hadn't stopped maybe the story would have gotten me back into it but I just didn't feel like going through so much useless attention-whoring to find the tiny flickers of story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15603482685751715498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WFVa1sEup6MYApXgEhhVDq2JUVKnK5L/HdtDkGBs/xZJ6MKjZSBtpAw3DLm2erHZjQy9/ujNUwosTHsXbmx7Aw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ICw3tBvK4t3WxSag+XQTfqinJh/3RHBK8doofdiUPaoxka/Bv8Qo2sLwv/ldFvepiCLKs7iisb/ATRD61pS5vw==')})
  }

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_28448877').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_28448877').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_28448877').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer4577392953278057841">John has always had a taste for wanderlust and adventure. As a young man, he travelled the world with little but what he could carry on his back. He has climbed Denali, hiked the Amazon, and even spent a year in Japan, teaching English and feeding deer in the famous Nara Park. His love of Asian history and philosophy has led him to become a master at Jeet Kune Do and a practicing Taoist.<br/><br/>John now d</span>
  <span id="freeText4577392953278057841" style="display:none">John has always had a taste for wanderlust and adventure. As a young man, he travelled the world with little but what he could carry on his back. He has climbed Denali, hiked the Amazon, and even spent a year in Japan, teaching English and feeding deer in the famous Nara Park. His love of Asian history and philosophy has led him to become a master at Jeet Kune Do and a practicing Taoist.<br /><br />John now divides his time between two homes, one in New York City, the other in London. He is married with a beautiful little girl who inspires and captivates him. They share their homes with a loyal, loving, German Shepherd. A man of many interests and talents, John has been a world-ranked tennis pro, a ballroom dancer, chef... and of course, he remains, and always will be a writer. All of John's many interests and adventures have inspired his writing. In addition, his imagination is so vivid and dear, it is almost as if he lives part-time within a third home in his mind, an inner world his readers glimpse when they read his novels.<br /><br />Unfortunately, he's still unable to get verified on Twitter and Facebook.<br /><br /><br />johnpatrickkennedy.net<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twitter.com/JohnPatKennedy">twitter.com/JohnPatKennedy</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://facebook.com/AuthorJohnPatrickKennedy/">facebook.com/AuthorJohnPatrickKennedy/</a></span>
